  <span id="freeText7059266038388273332" style="display:none"><b>December 24, 2011, 4:42 pm - Somewhere over the Pacific: In Which I Decided Not to Finish Reading Touch.</b><br /><br /><i>Technically speaking, this book was written flawlessly that it deserved a five star rating. But because Iâ€™m an emotional reader, the characterâ€™s actions and how he or she made me feel are usually directly proportionate to how I rate a book. Iâ€™m seething and I havenâ€™t even finished reading. Itâ€™s very unfortunate because this book had me entranced right up until the dreaded love triangle was introduced. After that, I was just pissed. I donâ€™t know if I should continue.<br /><br />I can understand the emotional state she was in. She was going through grief of different kinds and to be able to have something to anchor her down was a plausible, acceptable course of action. What she did, however, just infuriated me. I donâ€™t expect a perfect character but I do expect some consistencies in his or her traits. Why, oh why does love make us weak? Gah. Her sporadic childishness irked me. <br /><br />Nowadays, I wish books would come with a disclaimer: WARNING: LOVE TRIANGLE AHEAD. PROCEED WITH CAUTIONâ€¦OR RUN AS FAR AWAY AS YOU CAN.<br /><br />This review was frustrating to write. I loved Kale. I felt for him. I love his innocence and his intensity. I love reading about his wonders of the world he knew nothing about. And at the beginning of the novel, I have admired Dez. But things took a turn for the worse. Suddenly, Dezâ€™s actions and reasons started to grate on my nerves. Again, unfortunate because, seriously? This was a fantastic take on Marvel Comics' mutants. Nay, I say this book's genetically enhanced mutants has much better abilities than the X-Men. Yes, I went there. I love reading each one of the Sixesâ€™ powers. This novel is resonant of Shatter Me, only with more details and a lot more twists and ultimately - BETTER. Iâ€™m so mad that Iâ€™m letting that one element of the story get to me. It threw a monkey wrench on what had began as a great story.</i><br />__________________________________________________<br /><br /><b>December 24, 2011, 5:53 pm - Somewhere over the Pacific: Wherein I Ate Crow.</b> <br /><br />I always sound like an a$$ when I write something at the heat of the moment. But I'm a big enough person to admit when I'm wrong. This is one of those momentous occasions. I previously gave this book a ONE STAR rating and decided to flounced on it. But as I sat in my <i>Economy Plus</i> seat, going over this book in my head, there's this gnat of guilt that was quickly eating away at me. So I picked it up again and plowed on.<br /><br />I'm an idiot. I'm glad I kept going. If I were you, I'd completely ignore the first part of this review and go read this book. Love triangle <i>schmiangle.</i> I'm sorry this review is full of spoilers but I need to say what I needed to say. Touch is full of awesome - even with the love triangle, and hey, you know what? It wasn't even a LOVE TRIANGLE. So yes, don't let this deter you from reading this book. This book is action-packed, infused with romance that was sweet and sizzling for the most part. It's HEROES, X-MEN, SHATTER ME all rolled into one. This is definitely one of those can't-afford-to-miss reads. <br /></span>

  <span id="freeText6929706724493809948" style="display:none">My father was always evil. I knew it from the day I was born. He was always so empty, so cold! We were never able to have that regular father-daughter relationship. Plus, mumsy is gone. I'm so sad. (In a bid for attention, I do all sorts of crazy things like jumping off a 15 meter barn into a swimming pool. Notice me daddy dearest! I still long for your attention even though you are totally evil.) Ohh! A boy with cut feet who came out of nowhere. Better yet, he's HOT. (You're being chased by suspicious men? I feel your pain. Let's run away together!) Oh wait a second, now he's telling me that my father is evil. Silly Kale! I knew that a long time ago. You are simply so funny! Denazen, an evil thing my dad is a part of? Didn't I say he was evil? Ohh! You're called Sixes. That is so interesting. I can totally believe everything you say because it is so believable. I've known you for about 5 seconds. You're touch can kill? Funny! It doesn't seem to be affecting me. But guess what soul mate? I've got abilities too! Watch me morph different objects into different things. Unfortunately, it comes with horrible side effects of pain and nausea. What! My dad has my mom too? Now he has really crossed the line. There's a Six called Reaper who can help me break my mother out? Let's go find him! A price? I have to find the whole list of Sixes? Golly! I've got the perfect plan! I'll just tell my dad I'm a Six and morph stuff for him.  By the way, before I forget, I have an ex-boyfriend who still loves me. Love triangle or what? My father isn't the brightest bulb either. I guess it runs in the family.  Now, I realize that maybe I could have broken into Denazen without telling my dad about my ability. Silly me! <br /><br />BTW my cousin Brandt is totally awesome. But, now he's dead. I'll grieve for all of five seconds. 1,2,3,4,5. Okay, done! I'm ready to move on with life!<br /><br />Note: Since Kale has been away from civilization for so long, he's portrayed as very clueless about love. He says stuff like "I think I might be in love with you." Another example of something is "Can I hold your hand?" I found it really infuriating. If the author thought that making him clueless would make him have more appeal, she was very wrong. <br /><br />So, there you have it. I didn't like this book at all. Apparently, there's a second book. Joy! (NOT!)</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer400641854" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer235090259232853876">Touch is so bad.<br/><br/>The beginning was ok, i liked it. But it got worst and worst throughout the book.<br/><br/>The characters were plain and simple, no description and development. I could not connect with ANY one of them. Deznee ( main character) was so stupid, i hate her. Kale ( deznee's boyfriend) was even worst. He acted like he was 3 years old! He didn't know what holding hands means, and i know he was locked up since he was a kid, but seriously, who would believe that a 17 - 18 year old guy doesn't know</span>
  <span id="freeText235090259232853876" style="display:none">Touch is so bad.<br /><br />The beginning was ok, i liked it. But it got worst and worst throughout the book.<br /><br />The characters were plain and simple, no description and development. I could not connect with ANY one of them. Deznee ( main character) was so stupid, i hate her. Kale ( deznee's boyfriend) was even worst. He acted like he was 3 years old! He didn't know what holding hands means, and i know he was locked up since he was a kid, but seriously, who would believe that a 17 - 18 year old guy doesn't know the meaning of that, relationships and sex? Those 2 characters were so unrealistic. <br /><br />I wanted to finish this book, i was literally looking at the number of the page i was on, and begging for the end. I could not wait to finish this. To be honest, i skipped most of the pages.<br />The description of everything was just HORRIBLE! I was confused every second. One minute we have a kissing scene and then the next we find someone dead. What? <br /><br />The romance was the worst thing, i have never seen such a rushed love story. Page 50 and we have the first kiss between the main characters, and like 40 pages before one of them was trying to kill the other. I had a feeling that the only reason Kale was feeling anything for Deznne was because she was the only one that helped him and the only one that actually wouldn't die when he touched her. Oh, and Deznee's mother? It seemed to me like Kale was in love with her, he was all over her! And Deznee, she still had this 'little' thing for her ex boyfriend ( Alex) that cheated on her to ' protect her'. When Kale was gone, she literally jumped on Alex and started kissing him and making out. The she stopped because she finally realized that she was betraying Kale. But the next day, here we go again, she came back and starting making out again only to stop because the guilt was killing her inside. SHE. IS. SO. STUPID. Geese, i hate this book so much. <br /><br />I don't exactly know what really happened at the end, because i skipped pages. I was scared i'd fall asleep. Seriously, you shouldn't even think about buying this book, you will just waist your money and time. But on the other hand,, if your looking for something that will make you fall asleep, then you definitely found it. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3XPuhDC0PGBArC8IOxCJBZmbg5cafoiJvu+1IhPzNDJjV3JAeLF70Pbkg5cuLn5fw1PEbVOs90RvGgOBEYDnCA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ESCw/Wxq5KjNl+WfReaUAnKAIcr11U+XcCZI46CtrGOvBCw5JG+jGHvfSQBQ2GNYKEhmMLwHMFqh0/5Aot5/WQ==')})
  }
